     1→# PR Review Pipeline  
     2→  
     3→Three-phase PR review that catches what standard code audits miss. Spawns specialized agents  
     4→in sequence: correctness swarm, claim verification, skeptical review — then merges findings.  
     5→  
     6→## Use when  
     7→  
     8→- Before pushing a PR to an upstream repository  
     9→- After completing a feature branch and wanting a pre-merge quality gate  
    10→- When asked to "review the PR", "check the PR", "audit the PR", or "pre-merge review"  
    11→- After a swarm of code audit agents has already run (this catches what they miss)  
    12→  
    13→## Why this exists  
    14→  
    15→In a real incident, 20+ specialized audit agents checked a 40-file PR and found zero issues.  
    16→A single external reviewer then immediately found 3 real bugs — including a function that  
    17→claimed to populate 4 fields but actually populated zero of them. The audit swarm checked  
    18→code correctness per-file; the reviewer checked claims against reality.  
    19→  
    20→This pipeline automates the three complementary review perspectives needed to catch 100% of  
    21→issues:  
    22→  
    23→| Phase | Agent | What it catches | Analogy |  
    24→|-------|-------|-----------------|---------|  
    25→| 1 | Code Correctness (swarm) | Per-file bugs, type errors, security | Microscope |  
    26→| 2 | Claim Verification (single) | PR description lies, missing implementations | Fact-checker |  
    27→| 3 | Skeptical Review (single) | UX concerns, cross-file issues, design judgment | Telescope |  
    28→  
    29→## Protocol  
    30→  
    31→### Prerequisites  
    32→  
    33→Before starting, gather:  
    34→1. The PR number (or branch name)  
    35→2. The PR description text  
    36→3. The list of changed files grouped by domain  
    37→  
    38→### Phase 1: Code Correctness Swarm  
    39→  
    40→Spawn **one `epcp-code-correctness-agent` per domain** in parallel.  
    41→  
    42→Group changed files by domain. Common domain splits:  
    43→  
    44→| Domain | Fi

    23→## YOUR SCOPE AND LIMITATIONS

     2→name: epcp-claim-verification-agent  
     3→description: >

All fixes applied and validated. Here's what was fixed:  

| Issue | Before | After |  
|-------|--------|-------|  
| **Manifest filename** | `marketplace.json` | `plugin.json` |  
| **Manifest fields** | Non-standard `category`, `agents`, `skills`, `scripts` arrays | Standard fields only: `name`, `version`, `description`, `author`, `license`, `keywords` |  
| **Author format** | String `"Emasoft"` | Object `{name, url}` per spec |  
| **Agent frontmatter** | `name`, `model`, `tools` (non-standard) | `description`, `capabilities` (per spec) |  
| **SKILL.md** | No YAML frontmatter | Added `name`, `description`, `version` frontmatter |  

The plugin now follows the Claude Code plugin structure conventions. Component auto-discovery works via directory structure (agents/, skills/, scripts/), not via manifest arrays.

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-16 00:09:34]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

# /cpv-validate-agents Command  

Validates Claude Code agent definition files (markdown with YAML frontmatter).  

## Privacy Check (REQUIRED)  

Before running validation, ensure private path detection is configured:  

1. **Auto-detect username**: `python3 -c "import getpass; print(getpass.getuser())"`  
2. **If auto-detection fails**, ask the user for their system username  
3. **Pass to script**: `CLAUDE_PRIVATE_USERNAMES="username" uv run python scripts/...`  

## Usage  

```
/cpv-validate-agents <agent_path> [options]
```

## Arguments  

| Argument | Required | Description |  
|----------|----------|-------------|  
| `agent_path_or_name` | Yes | Path to agent .md file, directory, OR just the agent name for auto-discovery |  

### Auto-Discovery  

If you provide just a name (e.g., `my-agent`), the agent will search for it in:  
1. Agents folder (`./agents/my-agent.md`)  
2. Current directory (`./my-agent.md` if has agent frontmatter)  
3. OUTPUT_SKILLS plugins (`./OUTPUT_SKILLS/**/agents/my-agent.md`)  

If multiple matches are found, you'll be asked to choose.  

### Typo Tolerance  

Names are normalized before searching:  
- Converted to lowercase: `My-Agent` → `my-agent`  
- Underscores become hyphens: `my_agent` → `my-agent`  

If no exact match is found, fuzzy matching is used (e.g., `plugn-validator` → `plugin-validator`).  
**Fuzzy matches always require your confirmation before proceeding.**  

## Options  

| Option | Description |  
|--------|-------------|  
| `--verbose` | Show all checks including passed |  
| `--json` | Output results as JSON |  

## What Gets Validated  

### 1. YAML Frontmatter  
- Frontmatter exists (starts with `---`)  
- Valid YAML syntax  
- Closing `---` delimiter present  

### 2. Known Frontmatter Fields  
Valid agent frontmatter fields:  
- `name` - Agent identifier (kebab-case)  
- `description` - What the agent does  
- `tools` - Allowed tools list  
- `model` - Model specification (sonnet, opus, haiku)  
- `color` - UI color for agent  
- `capabilities` - Agent capabilities  
- `context` - Context mode (`fork`)  
- `agent` - Specialized agent type  
- `user-invocable` - Whether users can invoke directly  
- `system-prompt` - Custom system prompt  
- `skills` - List of skills the agent can use  

### 3. Name Validation  
- Maximum 64 characters  
- Must be lowercase  
- Must be kebab-case (letters, numbers, hyphens)  
- No consecutive hyphens  
- No leading/trailing hyphens  

### 4. Description Validation  
- Maximum 1024 characters  
- Non-empty recommended  
- Third-person voice recommended  
- "Use when" phrases encouraged  

### 5. Tools Validation  
- Space-delimited format  
- Validates against known tool names  
- Warns about unknown tools  

### 6. Model Validation  
Valid model values:  
- `sonnet` - Claude Sonnet (recommended)  
- `opus` - Claude Opus  
- `haiku` - Claude Haiku (note: less reliable for complex tasks)  
- `inherit` - Inherit from parent  

### 7. Context Field  
- Valid value: `fork` only  

### 8. Agent Types  
Valid specialized agent types:  
- `api-coordinator`  
- `test-engineer`  
- `deploy-agent`  
- `debug-  

... [1425 more chars truncated]  

</div>

---
name: pr-review-pipeline
description: >
  Three-phase PR review that catches what standard code audits miss.
  Trigger with "review the PR", "check the PR", "audit the PR", "pre-merge review".
version: 1.0.0
---

# PR Review Pipeline

## Overview

Three-phase PR review that catches what standard code audits miss. Spawns specialized agents
in sequence: correctness swarm, claim verification, skeptical review — then merges findings.

## Prerequisites

- `gh` CLI installed and authenticated (for `gh pr view`, `gh pr diff`)
- The PR must exist on GitHub (need PR number or branch name)
- `docs_dev/` directory must exist for report output
- The merge script at `~/.claude/plugins/emasoft-pr-checking-plugin/scripts/epcp-merge-reports.sh` must be executable

## Use when
```

   220→   appears once in the final report.  
   221→  
   222→5. **Exit code 1 = block the PR.** If the merge script returns exit code 1, there are  
   223→   MUST-FIX issues. Do not push the PR until they're resolved and the pipeline re-run.  
   224→  
   225→6. **Re-run after fixes.** After fixing issues, re-run the full pipeline to verify the fixes  
   226→   are correct and didn't introduce new issues.  
   227→  
   228→## Quick Reference  
   229→  
   230→```  
   231→# Full pipeline  
   232→/pr-review 206  
   233→  
   234→# Just claim verification (fastest, catches the most common misses)  
   235→# Spawn epcp-claim-verification-agent manually  
   236→  
   237→# Just skeptical review (for a quick holistic check)  
   238→# Spawn epcp-skeptical-reviewer-agent manually  
   239→```  
   240→  
   241→## Lessons Learned (Baked Into This Pipeline)  
   242→  
   243→1. **Swarms are microscopes.** Great at per-file correctness. Blind to the big picture.  
   244→2. **PR descriptions lie.** Not maliciously — authors believe they implemented what they described.  
   245→   The gap between intent and implementation is the #1 source of missed bugs.  
   246→3. **Absence is the hardest bug to find.** A missing field assignment produces no error, no warning,  
   247→   no test failure. The code compiles and runs fine. Only a claim verifier or skeptical reviewer  
   248→   will notice that `fromLabel` is declared in the type but never set in the return statement.  
   249→4. **Cross-file consistency requires holistic view.** Version "0.22.5" in JSON-LD but "0.22.4"  
   250→   in prose HTML — each file is internally valid, but together they're inconsistent.  
   251→5. **UX judgment is not a code concern.** Auto-copying clipboard on text selection is technically  
   252→   correct code. Whether it's a good idea requires a different kind of thinking.  
   253→6. **The stranger's perspective is irreplaceable.** Twenty agents who know the codebase missed  
   254→   what one agent pretending to be a stranger caught immediately

```
## Lessons Learned (Baked Into This Pipeline)

1. **Swarms are microscopes.** Great at per-file correctness. Blind to the big picture.
2. **PR descriptions lie.** Not maliciously — authors believe they implemented what they described.
   The gap between intent and implementation is the #1 source of missed bugs.
3. **Absence is the hardest bug to find.** A missing field assignment produces no error, no warning,
   no test failure. The code compiles and runs fine. Only a claim verifier or skeptical reviewer
   will notice that `fromLabel` is declared in the type but never set in the return statement.
4. **Cross-file consistency requires holistic view.** Version "0.22.5" in JSON-LD but "0.22.4"
   in prose HTML — each file is internally valid, but together they're inconsistent.
5. **UX judgment is not a code concern.** Auto-copying clipboard on text selection is technically
   correct code. Whether it's a good idea requires a different kind of thinking.
6. **The stranger's perspective is irreplaceable.** Twenty agents who know the codebase missed
   what one agent pretending to be a stranger caught immediately. Fresh eyes see what familiarity
   blinds you to.
```

**New:**  
```
## Instructions

Follow the 5-phase protocol strictly:

- [ ] Phase 1: Spawn code-correctness swarm (one agent per domain, parallel)
- [ ] Wait for all Phase 1 agents to complete
- [ ] Phase 2: Spawn single claim-verification agent
- [ ] Wait for Phase 2 to complete
- [ ] Phase 3: Spawn single skeptical-reviewer agent
- [ ] Wait for Phase 3 to complete
- [ ] Phase 4: Run merge script on all reports
- [ ] Phase 5: Present summary to user with verdict and issue counts

## Output

The pipeline produces:
- Per-domain correctness reports: `docs_dev/epcp-correctness-{domain}.md`
- Claim verification report: `docs_dev/epcp-claims.md`
- Skeptical review report: `docs_dev/epcp-review.md`


... [2299 more chars truncated]

     1→#!/bin/bash  
     2→# EPCP Merge Reports — Combines findings from all 3 review phases into one final report.  
     3→#  
     4→# Usage:  
     5→#   epcp-merge-reports.sh <output_dir> [report_glob_pattern]  
     6→#  
     7→# Arguments:  
     8→#   output_dir           Directory containing phase reports and where final report goes  
     9→#   report_glob_pattern  Optional glob pattern (default: "epcp-*.md")  
    10→#  
    11→# Expects reports named:  
    12→#   epcp-correctness-*.md  (Phase 1 — code correctness, may be multiple)  
    13→#   epcp-claims.md         (Phase 2 — claim verification)  
    14→#   epcp-review.md         (Phase 3 — skeptical review)  
    15→#  
    16→# Output:  
    17→#   pr-review-YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS.md  (merged final report)  
    18→#  
    19→# Exit codes:  
    20→#   0 — No MUST-FIX issues found  
    21→#   1 — MUST-FIX issues found (PR needs changes before merge)  
    22→#   2 — Error (missing reports, invalid input)  
    23→  
    24→set -eo pipefail  
    25→  
    26→# ── Configuration ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────  
    27→RED='\033[0;31m'  
    28→GREEN='\033[0;32m'  
    29→YELLOW='\033[1;33m'  
    30→CYAN='\033[0;36m'  
    31→NC='\033[0m'  
    32→  
    33→OUTPUT_DIR="${1:-.}"  
    34→PATTERN="${2:-epcp-*.md}"  
    35→TIMESTAMP=$(date +%Y-%m-%d-%H%M%S)  
    36→FINAL_REPORT="${OUTPUT_DIR}/pr-review-${TIMESTAMP}.md"  
    37→  
    38→# ── Validate input ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────  
    39→if [ ! -d "$OUTPUT_DIR" ]; then  
    40→    echo -e "${RED}Error: Output directory '${OUTPUT_DIR}' does not exist${NC}"  
    41→    exit 2  
    42→fi  
    43→  
    44→# Find all phase reports  
    45→REPORTS=()  
    46→while IFS= read -r -d '' file; do  
    47→    REPORTS+=("$file")  
    48→done < <(find "$OUTPUT_DIR" -maxdepth 1 -name "$PATTERN" -print0 | sort -z)  
    49→  
    50→if [ ${#REPORTS[@]} -eq 0 ]; then  
    51→    echo -e "${RED}Error: No reports matching '${PATTERN}' found in '${OUTPUT_DIR}'${NC}"  
    52→    exit 2  
    53→f

    if [[ "$report_name" == epcp-correctness-* ]]; then
        PHASE="Phase 1: Code Correctness"
    elif [[ "$report_name" == epcp-claims* ]]; then
        PHASE="Phase 2: Claim Verification"
    elif [[ "$report_name" == epcp-review* ]]; then
        PHASE="Phase 3: Skeptical Review"
    fi

    # Extract MUST-FIX sections
    in_section=""
    current_finding=""
    finding_id=""
```

**New:**  
```
    # Extract MUST-FIX sections
    in_section=""
    finding_id=""
```

## CRITICAL RULES

1. **Read the ENTIRE diff.** Not just changed files — the full diff gives you context about
   what was added, removed, and modified together.
2. **Think like a user.** Not like a compiler. "Will this surprise someone?" is a valid question.
3. **Think like a maintainer.** "Will this be easy to debug in 6 months?" is a valid question.
4. **Cross-reference everything.** Version in file A should match version in file B. Interface
   in types/ should match implementation in lib/.
5. **Check the gaps.** The most dangerous bugs are in what's NOT there — missing fields,
   missing error handling, missing validation, missing tests.
6. **Minimal report to orchestrator.** Write full details to the report file. Return to the
   orchestrator ONLY: `[DONE] skeptical-review - Verdict: {verdict}, {N} issues ({M} must-fix). Report: {path}`

     8→  
     9→# PR Review Pipeline  
    10→  
    11→## Overview  
    12→  
    13→Three-phase PR review that catches what standard code audits miss. Spawns specialized agents  
    14→in sequence: correctness swarm, claim verification, skeptical review — then merges findings.  
    15→  
    16→## Prerequisites  
    17→  
    18→- `gh` CLI installed and authenticated (for `gh pr view`, `gh pr diff`)  
    19→- The PR must exist on GitHub (need PR number or branch name)  
    20→- `docs_dev/` directory must exist for report output  
    21→- The merge script at `~/.claude/plugins/emasoft-pr-checking-plugin/scripts/epcp-merge-reports.sh` must be executable  
    22→  
    23→## Use when  
    24→  
    25→- Before pushing a PR to an upstream repository  
    26→- After completing a feature branch and wanting a pre-merge quality gate  
    27→- When asked to "review the PR", "check the PR", "audit the PR", or "pre-merge review"  
    28→- After a swarm of code audit agents has already run (this catches what they miss)  
    29→  
    30→## Why this exists

**Result:**

   215→  
   216→3. **Each agent writes to a file.** Agents return only 1-2 lines to the orchestrator.  
   217→   Full findings go in the report files. This prevents context flooding.  
   218→  
   219→4. **The merge script deduplicates.** If Phase 1 and Phase 3 find the same issue, it only  
   220→   appears once in the final report.  
   221→  
   222→5. **Exit code 1 = block the PR.** If the merge script returns exit code 1, there are  
   223→   MUST-FIX issues. Do not push the PR until they're resolved and the pipeline re-run.  
   224→  
   225→6. **Re-run after fixes.** After fixing issues, re-run the full pipeline to verify the fixes  
   226→   are correct and didn't introduce new issues.  
   227→  
   228→## Quick Reference  
   229→  
   230→```  
   231→# Full pipeline  
   232→/pr-review 206  
   233→  
   234→# Just claim verification (fastest, catches the most common misses)  
   235→# Spawn epcp-claim-verification-agent manually  
   236→  
   237→# Just skeptical review (for a quick holistic check)  
   238→# Spawn epcp-skeptical-reviewer-agent manually  
   239→```  
   240→  
   241→## Instructions  
   242→  
   243→Follow the 5-phase protocol strictly:  
   244→

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 00:17:35]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `SKILL.md`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/.claude/plugins/emasoft-pr-checking-plugin/skills/pr-review/SKILL.md`  

**Old:**  
```
## Instructions

Follow the 5-phase protocol strictly:

- [ ] Phase 1: Spawn code-correctness swarm (one agent per domain, parallel)
- [ ] Wait for all Phase 1 agents to complete
- [ ] Phase 2: Spawn single claim-verification agent
- [ ] Wait for Phase 2 to complete
- [ ] Phase 3: Spawn single skeptical-reviewer agent
- [ ] Wait for Phase 3 to complete
- [ ] Phase 4: Run merge script on all reports
- [ ] Phase 5: Present summary to user with verdict and issue counts
```

**New:**  
```
## Instructions

Follow the 5-phase protocol strictly:

1. Gather the PR number, description, and list of changed files grouped by domain.
2. Spawn one `epcp-code-correctness-agent` per domain in parallel (Phase 1 swarm).
3. Wait for all Phase 1 agents to complete before proceeding.
4. Spawn a single `epcp-claim-verification-agent` with the PR description and commit messages (Phase 2).
5. Wait for Phase 2 to complete before proceeding.
6. Spawn a single `epcp-skeptical-reviewer-agent` with the full diff and earlier reports (Phase 3).
7. Wait for Phase 3 to complete.
8. Run the merge script: `bash ~/.claude/plugins/emasoft-pr-checking-plugin/scripts/epcp-merge-reports.sh docs_dev/`
9. Read the final merged report and present the verdict summary to the user.
10. If exit code 1 (MUST-FIX issues), do NOT push the PR until issues are resolved and pipeline re-run.
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/.claude/plugins/emasoft-pr-checking-plugin/skills/pr-review/SKILL.md has been updated successfully.

**Result:**

     1→# emasoft-pr-checking-plugin  
     2→  
     3→Three-phase PR review pipeline for Claude Code. Catches bugs that standard code audits miss by cross-referencing PR claims against actual implementation.  
     4→  
     5→## Installation  
     6→  
     7→This plugin is installed as a local Claude Code plugin:  
     8→  
     9→```bash  
    10→# The plugin is already at $CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT/  
    11→# Claude Code auto-discovers it from the plugins directory.  
    12→# No additional installation steps required.  
    13→```  
    14→  
    15→Ensure the merge script is executable:  
    16→  
    17→```bash  
    18→chmod +x $CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT/scripts/epcp-merge-reports.sh  
    19→```  
    20→  
    21→## Agents  
    22→  
    23→| Agent | Role | Spawning |  
    24→|-------|------|----------|  
    25→| `epcp-code-correctness-agent` | Per-file correctness audit | Swarm (one per domain) |  
    26→| `epcp-claim-verification-agent` | PR claim vs code verification | Single instance |  
    27→| `epcp-skeptical-reviewer-agent` | Holistic external review | Single instance |  
    28→  
    29→## Usage  
    30→  
    31→Activate the `pr-review-pipeline` skill by asking Claude to review a PR:  
    32→  
    33→```text  
    34→review PR 206  
    35→```  
    36→  
    37→The skill orchestrates all 3 phases automatically and produces a merged report.  
    38→  
    39→## Pipeline  
    40→  
    41→1. **Phase 1** - Code correctness swarm (parallel, one agent per domain)  
    42→2. **Phase 2** - Claim verification (sequential, single agent)  
    43→3. **Phase 3** - Skeptical review (sequential, single agent)  
    44→4. **Phase 4** - Merge reports via `scripts/epcp-merge-reports.sh`  
    45→5. **Phase 5** - Present verdict to user  
    46→  
    47→## License  
    48→  
    49→MIT  
    50→

Three-phase PR review pipeline for Claude Code. Catches bugs that standard code audits miss by cross-referencing PR claims against actual implementation.

     1→---  
     2→name: PR Review Pipeline  
     3→description: >  
     4→  Three-phase PR review that catches what standard code audits miss. Use when reviewing PRs,  
     5→  auditing code changes, or performing pre-merge quality gates. Triggers on "review the PR",  
     6→  "check the PR", "audit the PR", "pre-merge review".  
     7→version: 1.0.0  
     8→---  
     9→  
    10→# PR Review Pipeline  
    11→  
    12→Three-phase PR review that catches what standard code audits miss. Spawns specialized agents  
    13→in sequence: correctness swarm, claim verification, skeptical review — then merges findings.  
    14→  
    15→## Use when  
    16→  
    17→- Before pushing a PR to an upstream repository  
    18→- After completing a feature branch and wanting a pre-merge quality gate  
    19→- When asked to "review the PR", "check the PR", "audit the PR", or "pre-merge review"  
    20→- After a swarm of code audit agents has already run (this catches what they miss)  
    21→  
    22→## Why this exists  
    23→  
    24→In a real incident, 20+ specialized audit agents checked a 40-file PR and found zero issues.  
    25→A single external reviewer then immediately found 3 real bugs — including a function that  
    26→claimed to populate 4 fields but actually populated zero of them. The audit swarm checked  
    27→code correctness per-file; the reviewer checked claims against reality.  
    28→  
    29→This pipeline automates the three complementary review perspectives needed to catch 100% of  
    30→issues:  
    31→  
    32→| Phase | Agent | What it catches | Analogy |  
    33→|-------|-------|-----------------|---------|  
    34→| 1 | Code Correctness (swarm) | Per-file bugs, type errors, security | Microscope |  
    35→| 2 | Claim Verification (single) | PR description lies, missing implementations | Fact-checker |  
    36→| 3 | Skeptical Review (single) | UX concerns, cross-file issues, design judgment | Telescope |  
    37→  
    38→## Protocol  
    39→  
    40→### Prerequisites  
    41→  
    42→Before starting,

     1→---  
     2→description: >  
     3→  Extracts every factual claim from the PR description and commit message, then verifies  
     4→  each one against the actual code. This agent catches the #1 source of missed bugs:  
     5→  the gap between what the author thinks they did and what the code actually does.  
     6→  Born from a real incident where "fromLabel/toLabel population via registry lookup" was  
     7→  claimed in the PR description but never implemented in convertAMPToMessage().  
     8→capabilities:  
     9→  - Extract structured claims from PR descriptions and commit messages  
    10→  - Verify each claim against actual source code by reading full functions  
    11→  - Trace data flow to confirm fields are populated, assigned, and returned

    13→  - Detect scaffolded-but-not-wired features, incomplete renames, dead type fields  
    14→---  
    15→  
    16→# EPCP Claim Verification Agent  
    17→  
    18→You are a claim verification auditor. Your job is to read the PR description and commit  
    19→message, extract every factual claim the author makes about what the code does, then  
    20→systematically verify each claim against the actual source code.  
    21→  
    22→## WHY YOU EXIST
